#DDDDFF; color: black">Statistics (2020 Jan-Nov)</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><table class="infobox-subbox"><tbody><tr><th scope="row" style="background-color: #eee"><td colspan="2" class="infobox-full-data"><div style="text-align: left;">Sources: MAG Manchester Airports Group website, UK <a href="/wiki/Aeronautical_Information_Publication" title="Aeronautical Information Publication">AIP</a> at <a href="/wiki/National_Air_Traffic_Services" class="mw-redirect" title="National Air Traffic Services">NATS</a><sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><br />Statistics from the <a href="/wiki/Civil_Aviation_Authority_(United_Kingdom)" title="Civil Aviation Authority (United Kingdom)">UK Civil Aviation Authority</a><sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Manchester Airport</b> (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>MAN</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EGCC</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> at <a href="/wiki/Ringway,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringway, Manchester">Ringway, Manchester</a>, England, 7.5 <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical miles</a> (13.9&#160;km; 8.6&#160;mi) south-west of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_city_centre" title="Manchester city centre">Manchester city centre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> In 2019, it was the <a href="/wiki/List_of_busiest_airports_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of busiest airports in the United Kingdom">third busiest airport</a> in the United Kingdom in terms of passenger numbers and the busiest of those not serving <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The airport comprises three passenger <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminals</a> and a cargo terminal, and is the only airport in the UK other than <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">Heathrow Airport</a> to operate two runways over 3,280&#160;yd (2,999&#160;m) in length. Manchester Airport covers an area of 560 hectares (1,400 acres) and has flights to 199 destinations, placing the airport thirteenth globally for total destinations served.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Officially opened on 25 June 1938,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> it was initially known as Ringway Airport, and is still called this locally. In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, as <a href="/wiki/RAF_Ringway" title="RAF Ringway">RAF Ringway</a>, it was a base for the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a>. The airport is owned and managed by the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_Holdings" title="Manchester Airport Holdings">Manchester Airport Holdings</a> (trading as <i>MAG</i>), a holding company owned by the Australian finance house IFM Investors and the ten metropolitan borough councils of <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester" title="Greater Manchester">Greater Manchester</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Manchester_City_Council" title="Manchester City Council">Manchester City Council</a> owning the largest stake. <a href="/wiki/Ringway,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringway, Manchester">Ringway</a>, after which the airport was named, is a village with a few buildings and church at the southern edge of the airport.\n</p><p>Future developments include the \xc2\xa3800 million <a href="/wiki/Airport_City_Manchester" title="Airport City Manchester">Airport City Manchester</a> logistics, manufacturing, office and hotel space next to the airport. Ongoing and future transport improvements include the \xc2\xa3290 million <a href="/wiki/A555_road" title="A555 road">Eastern Link</a> relief road, which opened in October 2018. A <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> station known as <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Interchange" title="Manchester Interchange">Manchester Interchange</a>, earmarked for opening in 2033, will create a regular sub-10-minute shuttle service for connecting rail passengers between <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">central Manchester</a> and the Airport while relieving stress on the <a href="/wiki/Styal_Line" title="Styal Line">Styal Line</a> to the Airport from Manchester which has become one of the most congested routes on the <a href="/wiki/National_Rail" title="National Rail">National Rail</a> network.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the airport handled a record 27.8 million passengers in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> it is currently undergoing a major expansion programme to double the size of Terminal 2, with the first elements opening in 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> The \xc2\xa31 billion expansion will be completed in 2024 and enable the Terminal 2 to handle 35 million passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Capacity exists for up to 50 million passengers annually with two runways,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> however this potential figure is limited by the airport\'s restriction to 61 aircraft movements per hour as well as existing terminal sizes to effectively process arrivals and departures.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Manchester_Airport" title="History of Manchester Airport">History of Manchester Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ringway,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringway, Manchester">Ringway, Manchester</a></div>\n<h3><span id="Construction_.26_Early_years_of_operation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_&amp;_Early_years_of_operation">Construction &amp; Early years of operation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Construction &amp; Early years of operation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Construction commenced on 28 November 1935 with the airport partially operational by June 1937, with full construction completed on 25 June 1938, in <a href="/wiki/Ringway,_Manchester" class="mw-redirect" title="Ringway, Manchester">Ringway</a> parish.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Its northern border was Yewtree Lane between Firtree Farm and The Grange, east of the crossroads marked "Ringway", and its southeast border a little west of Altrincham Road, along the lane from Oversleyford running northeast then east into <a href="/wiki/Styal" title="Styal">Styal</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 1938, <a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> became the first airline to launch scheduled commercial flights to Manchester<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/RAF_Ringway" title="RAF Ringway">RAF Ringway</a> was important in military aircraft production and training <a href="/wiki/Parachuting" title="Parachuting">parachutists</a>. After the Second World War, the base reverted to a civilian airport and gradually expanded to its present size. Manchester Airport was the busiest airport after Heathrow following the war.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1940.27s_.26_50.27s_-_Post_War_Era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1940\'s_&amp;_50\'s_-_Post_War_Era">1940\'s &amp; 50\'s - Post War Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1940&#039;s &amp; 50&#039;s - Post War Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1946, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> began operations from Manchester, following the commencement of peacetime passenger services form the airport, and remains the airports longest continuous operator, celebrating 75 years of service in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> In 1953, Manchester commenced 24 hour operations, with the ability to handle flights during the day and night, which helped the airport handle 163,000 passengers. 1953 also saw the commencement of intercontinental flights by <a href="/wiki/Sabena" title="Sabena">Sabena Belgian</a> to New York, followed closely by the launch of services to New York by <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">BOAC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1960.27s_.26_70.27s_-_Jet_Era"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1960\'s_&amp;_70\'s_-_Jet_Era">1960\'s &amp; 70\'s - Jet Era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1960&#039;s &amp; 70&#039;s - Jet Era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:5_classics_1_shot!.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg/220px-5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg/330px-5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg/440px-5_classics_1_shot%21.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="666" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:5_classics_1_shot!.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Apron view, 1972</div></div></div>\n<p>1963 saw the introduction of the first transatlantic flight to originate at Manchester. The thrice weekly service was operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">British Overseas Air Corporation</a> (BOAC) using a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_707" title="Boeing 707">Boeing 707</a> via <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Prestwick_Airport" title="Glasgow Prestwick Airport">Prestwick</a>. During 1969, the Runway was extended to 2,745 metres, allowing aircraft to take off with a full payload and fly non-stop to Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1971, The airport reached a milestone of handling over 2 million passengers in one year. The following year saw the opening of a link road, connecting the airport to the <a href="/wiki/M56_motorway" title="M56 motorway">M56</a> Motorway, improving road access from Manchester, Cheshire &amp; North Wales.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> During 1975, Ringway was officially renamed to Manchester International Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1980.27s_.26_90.27s_-_Further_growth_.26_expansion"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1980\'s_&amp;_90\'s_-_Further_growth_&amp;_expansion">1980\'s &amp; 90\'s - Further growth &amp; expansion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1980&#039;s &amp; 90&#039;s - Further growth &amp; expansion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manchester Airport saw rapid growth and expansion during the 80\'s &amp; 90\'s which shaped the airport for the coming decades. Many of the developments made during this period remain in place or have only recently been altered following the introduction of the Manchester Transformation Project. In 1987 the airport saw continued growth in passenger numbers, reaching the milestone of handing one million passengers a month for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> This growth boosted expansion plans, including planning for a new terminal. The following year, in 1988 Manchester celebrated its <a href="/wiki/Golden_jubilee" title="Golden jubilee">Golden Jubilee</a>.\n</p><p>\n1989 saw the official opening of Terminal A, which now forms part of Terminal 3, by <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a>. In 1993, Terminal 2 was officially opened by the <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Duke of Edinburgh</a> along with the official opening of <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport station</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> From 1997 to 2001, a second runway was constructed, causing large-scale protests in <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a>, especially in the village of <a href="/wiki/Styal" title="Styal">Styal</a> where natural habitats were disturbed and listed buildings demolished to make space for construction.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg/220px-Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg/330px-Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg/440px-Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1275" data-file-height="1275" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Aa_oldwythenshawe_00.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map of the area where <b>Manchester Airport</b> is located, <b>Circa 1925</b></div></div></div>\n<h3><span id="2000.27s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2000\'s">2000\'s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2000&#039;s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>During the early 2000s British Airways scaled down operations from Manchester Airport with the sale of their <a href="/wiki/BA_Connect" title="BA Connect">BA Connect</a> subsidiary to <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> and the ending of their franchise agreement with <a href="/wiki/GB_Airways" title="GB Airways">GB Airways</a>, a business subsequently sold to <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">EasyJet</a>. In October 2008, the daily <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York\xe2\x80\x93JFK</a> service was terminated and in March 2013 the daily to <a href="/wiki/Gatwick_Airport" title="Gatwick Airport">London Gatwick</a> was ended, although the service has resumed in recent years.\n</p><p>Since taking over <a href="/wiki/BA_Connect" title="BA Connect">BA Connect</a>\'s select routes, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> has gone on to add several more destinations. In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> introduced the "mini hub" concept co-ordinating the arrival and departure times of various domestic services throughout the day and thereby creating combinations such as Norwich-Manchester-Belfast, Glasgow-Manchester-Southampton and Edinburgh-Manchester-Exeter with conveniently short transfer times.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2010.27s"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2010\'s">2010\'s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2010&#039;s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>2010 saw the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, which continues to operate the aircraft up to 3 times daily on its route to <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a>\n</p><p>In 2013, Manchester Airport celebrated its 75th Anniversary. It also saw the completion and opening of the newly constructed <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control tower</a> - which is now located in an independent tower, not on top of the airport as previously located. 2013 also saw <a href="/wiki/Airport_City_Manchester" title="Airport City Manchester">Airport City Manchester</a> gain planning approval.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> During 2013, <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> introduced its <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic_Little_Red" title="Virgin Atlantic Little Red">Little Red</a> short-haul brand to take-up some of the available Heathrow and Gatwick slots, which resulted from <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">BMI</a> ceasing operations. Manchester was the inaugural destination, with services were operated by aircraft leased from <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>. However, these services ceased in March 2015 due to low popularity.<sup id="cite_ref-Little_Red_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Little_Red-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014, the Manchester Airport Metrolink route launched as part of the route expansion plans of the Manchester <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Metrolink</a> tramway, aiding transport to and from the airport to the city center.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_13-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2019, The first phase of the new Terminal 2 extension was completed with Pier 1 opening on April 1, 2019. The second phase of the extension plan was due to open in 2020, however this has been delayed due to <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="COVID-19 pandemic in the United Kingdom">COVID-19</a><sup id="cite_ref-:1_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the later part of the decade <a href="/wiki/Monarch_Airlines" title="Monarch Airlines">Monarch Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Airlines">Thomas Cook Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Flybe" title="Flybe">Flybe</a> all entered administration and ceased operations, having a major impact on local employment &amp; operations at Manchester, as well as leaving thousands of passengers stranded - many abroad. Monarch Airlines was an operator at Manchester between 1981 and 2017. The airline operated short and medium flights to Europe, and had its own maintenance base at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> It entered administration and ceased operations in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Thomas Cook Airlines was a major operator at Manchester, it operated scheduled and charter flights to over 50 destinations in Europe, America and the Caribbean. Its parent company also held a maintenance base at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The airline entered compulsory liquidation in September 2019, with many aircraft left parked at the airport whilst payment disputes were carried out.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Flybe was a British airline, which had a significant base at Manchester, which provided more than half of UK domestic flights outside London. Plans were formulated by a consortium Including <a href="/wiki/Stobart_Air" title="Stobart Air">Stobart Air</a> &amp; <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Atlantic" title="Virgin Atlantic">Virgin Atlantic</a> to save FlyBe with the launch of <a href="/wiki/Connect_Airways" title="Connect Airways">Connect Airways</a>, however plans were dropped in early 2020 &amp; all operations ceased.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2020s">2020s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2020s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Like most British and International airports, Manchester has been severely affected by the global Coronavirus pandemic and the subsequent reduction in air passengers. A number of airlines ceased, paused or reduced routes to the airport. The reduced passenger numbers saw the temporary closure of both Terminals 2 &amp; 3.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>, which previously operated a Manchester-Atlanta service, until 29 March 2015 (when partner airline Virgin Atlantic began to operate the route)<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> announced plans to return to Manchester in Summer 2020 with flights to <a href="/wiki/Logan_International_Airport" title="Logan International Airport">Boston</a>, using a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_757" title="Boeing 757">Boeing 757</a>. These plans were later dropped due to low passenger numbers caused by the global pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In late 2020 <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> announced that its daily flights to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia</a> would cease operation amid ongoing travel disruption caused by the global <a href="/wiki/Coronavirus_disease_2019" class="mw-redirect" title="Coronavirus disease 2019">Coronavirus</a> outbreak.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> The departure of American Airlines also marked the final US based airline at Manchester. American Airlines had previously operated services to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York</a>, <a href="/wiki/O%27Hare_International_Airport" title="O&#39;Hare International Airport">Chicago</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Douglas_International_Airport" title="Charlotte Douglas International Airport">Charlotte</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Data recorded and published by the Civil Aviation Authority (CAA) show that during the first 11 months (January through November) of 2020, passenger \'Terminal &amp; Transit\' numbers dropped from 29,374,282 in 2019 to 6,787,127 in 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Future">Future</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Future">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Airport_City_Manchester" title="Airport City Manchester">Airport City Manchester</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg/220px-Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="93" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg/330px-Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg/440px-Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5772" data-file-height="2437" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_Panorama_September_2014.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Manchester Airport viewed from the south-west</div></div></div>\n<p>As part of the Government\'s <a href="/wiki/Environmental_impact_of_aviation_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Environmental impact of aviation in the United Kingdom">Future of Air Transport</a> <a href="/wiki/White_paper" title="White paper">White Paper</a>, Manchester Airport published its Master Plan on its proposed expansions until 2030.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Demolition of older buildings, such as old storage buildings, the old Alpha Catering Building and Males Garage, to the east of Terminal 2 has already begun, to make way for a new apron and taxiway towards runway 05L/23R and an eastwards extension of Terminal 2, which is planned to provide fifteen more covered stands.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The World Logistics Hub is also part of the Airport City Enterprise Developments in south Manchester. This development is designed to meet the growing demand for cargo handling space and infrastructure outside of the southeast.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Positioned on the southwest side of the <a href="/wiki/A538_road" title="A538 road">A538 road</a>, next to the southeast side of the <a href="/wiki/M56_motorway" title="M56 motorway">M56 motorway</a> across the A538 from the World Freight Terminal, it provides access to the trunk motorway network via Junction 6.\n</p><p>Manchester Airport has development plans to meet the growing demand to fly. One document, "The Need for Land", outlines several development ideas. Five affected areas are:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Area A</i> is a triangle of land between the <a href="/wiki/A538_road" title="A538 road">A538 road</a> and Runway 1 and the cargo terminal which is currently under development. It will be used together with <i>Area E</i>, a triangle of land west of the A538 up to the M56, with its west corner opposite Warburton Green, for the expansion of aircraft maintenance, vehicle maintenance/storage and cargo handling. The \xe2\x80\x98Clough Bank\xe2\x80\x99 and \xe2\x80\x98Cotterill Clough\xe2\x80\x99 areas are being enhanced with mitigation areas that will become part of the extensive Landscape Habitat Management Area. The A538 alignment to be retained and capacity has been added, as required, to meet increased traffic volumes.</li>\n<li><i>Area B</i> is located north of Ringway Road and east of Shadow Moss Road, car park has been provided to replace spaces lost to the Airport City development and Apron/Terminal expansion.</li>\n<li><i>Area C</i> consists of several areas of land mainly inside the <a href="/wiki/M56_motorway" title="M56 motorway">M56</a> / M56 spur junction, around Hasty Lane east of M56 and around the current M56 spur. The land will be used for hotels and office space<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 1\'s current capacity is around 11 million passengers a year,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> compared with an annual capacity of 2.5&#160;million passengers when it first opened.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>In the Summer of 2009, a \xc2\xa350&#160;million redevelopment programme for Terminal 1 was completed as well as the construction of new car parking facilities and taxiways for aircraft.\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Area D</i> are areas of land on both sides of Manchester Airport railway spur, at Smithy Farm and east of B5166 Styal Road around and inside railway spur junction where car parking, offices, hotel, etc. can be developed.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger_terminals">Passenger terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Passenger terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_T1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_T1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" data-file-width="4896" data-file-height="3672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Terminal_2,_Manchester_Airport,_June_2016_(02).JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Check-in hall at Terminal 2</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg/220px-Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg/330px-Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg/440px-Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dusk_at_Terminal_3_-_geograph.org.uk_-_610450.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal 3</div></div></div>\n<p>Manchester Airport has three passenger terminals (Terminals 1, 2 and 3). Terminals 1 and 2 are linked by the <a href="/wiki/Skyway" title="Skyway"><i>skylink</i></a>, with <a href="/wiki/Moving_walkway" title="Moving walkway">travelators</a> to aid passengers with the 10\xe2\x80\x9315-minute walk. Terminal 3 is linked to Terminal 1 and the <i>skylink</i> by a covered walkway. The <i>"skylink"</i> also connects the terminals to the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">airport railway station</a> complex (known as <i>"The Station"</i>) and the <a href="/wiki/Radisson_Blu" title="Radisson Blu">Radisson BLU Hotel</a>. Skylink 1 started construction in 1991 and opened 1993. Skylink 2 opened in September 1996 along with the Radisson.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 1 is used by airlines with scheduled and charter operations, flying to European and other worldwide destinations. It is the largest terminal at the airport. It was opened in 1962, by <a href="/wiki/Prince_Philip,_Duke_of_Edinburgh" title="Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh">Prince Philip, Duke of Edinburgh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-facelift_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facelift-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> and it is a base for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jet2" class="mw-redirect" title="Jet2">Jet2</a>. Some other airlines that fly out of Terminal 1 include <a href="/wiki/Icelandair" title="Icelandair">Icelandair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_Transat" title="Air Transat">Air Transat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Titan_Airways" title="Titan Airways">Titan Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Etihad_Airways" title="Etihad Airways">Etihad Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Airlines" title="Scandinavian Airlines">Scandinavian Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swiss_International_Air_Lines" title="Swiss International Air Lines">Swiss International Air Lines</a>, <a href="/wiki/TAP_Air_Portugal" title="TAP Air Portugal">TAP Air Portugal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>. Terminal 1 is spread over an area of 110,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (1,200,000&#160;sq&#160;ft).\n</p><p>The terminal has 2 piers which combined have 29 stands, of which 15 have air bridges and is the largest of the three terminals. Gate 12 was specially adapted to accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> which is operated by <a href="/wiki/Emirates_(airline)" title="Emirates (airline)">Emirates</a> on their route three times per day from <a href="/wiki/Dubai_International_Airport" title="Dubai International Airport">Dubai</a> to Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Terminal 1\'s current capacity is around 11 million passengers a year,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_34-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> compared with an annual capacity of 2.5&#160;million passengers when it first opened.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_34-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the Summer of 2009, a \xc2\xa350&#160;million redevelopment programme for Terminal 1 was completed, which included a new \xc2\xa314&#160;million 14-lane security area.<sup id="cite_ref-Manchester_Airport_\xc2\xa350m_overhaul_complete_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Manchester_Airport_\xc2\xa350m_overhaul_complete-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Passenger flow on Terminal 1\'s gating piers is due to be realigned, with plans to redesign the piers so departures and arrivals do not contraflow on the same level, allowing larger seating areas at the gates, express retail outlets and a dedicated lounge and gating area for future <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a> flights. Currently only Gate 12, Pier B, has been upgraded to accommodate the A380. Part of this work saw the removal of the South Bay remote aircraft stands, constructed in 1962 between taxiways Juliet and Kilo and more recently re-aligning taxiway Juliet into an extended taxiway Bravo.\n</p><p>Terminal 1 will not be included in the 10 Year Airport expansion project and will be closed and demolished by around 2022. However Piers B and C in Terminal 1 are due to be kept with Pier B due to be entirely rebuilt.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal 2 is used by a variety of airlines, operating both charter and scheduled flights to many European and worldwide destinations.\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is spread over an area of 52,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (560,000&#160;sq&#160;ft). Terminal 2 has 16 gates, of which 20 have air bridges. The design of the terminal makes it capable of extensive expansion; building work has begun for an extension providing additional gates, together with the construction of a satellite pier. Terminal 2\'s current capacity is around 8&#160;million passengers a year, this will be extended to ultimately handle 25&#160;million passengers a year.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated7_34-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated7-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, an \xc2\xa311&#160;million project commenced to redevelop Terminal 2 by improving security facilities and enhancing retail and catering services.\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is due to receive a major extension, to encompass current remote stands to the west. Between twelve and fifteen covered aircraft stands will be made available by this. An air side link for transferring passengers between Terminals 1 and 2 is at the planning stage, designed in an effort to boost Manchester\'s chances of becoming a major hub airport and minimise missed connections. It was announced in June 2015 that the airport would have an expansion taking 10 years to complete. Terminal 2 will be the most developed, adding new piers to the terminal and also create a larger security hall as well as more outlets. There will also be a connecting hallway to Terminal 3.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_News_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_News-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first phase of the new extension, Pier 1, opened on 1 April 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n<sup id="cite_ref-:2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> The second phase, the terminal extension, was due to open in April 2020 but has been delayed due to the impacts of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. The current Terminal 2 will then close for two years for refurbishment.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_3">Terminal 3</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Terminal 3">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Terminal A (a self contained new domestic terminal to replace the original pier A) was opened in 1989 by <a href="/wiki/Diana,_Princess_of_Wales" title="Diana, Princess of Wales">Diana, Princess of Wales</a> and had many names before final being expanded and a re-designation as Terminal 3 in May 1998.\nThe terminal was known in succession as "Terminal A"; "Terminal A \xe2\x80\x93 Domestic"; "Terminal 1A" after Terminal 2 opened in 1993; "Terminal 1A \xe2\x80\x93 British Airways and Domestic"; "Terminal 3 \xe2\x80\x93 British Airways and Domestic" before becoming simply known as Terminal 3 in 1998. In June 1998, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a> opened their new \xc2\xa375&#160;million terminal facility designed by <a href="/wiki/Grimshaw_Architects" title="Grimshaw Architects">Grimshaw Architects</a>, this being a major extension to Terminal A and became the primary user of the terminal along with codeshare partner airlines (<a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld Alliance</a>). Terminal 3 now spreads over an area of 44,400&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (478,000&#160;sq&#160;ft).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="PremiAir_VIP_terminal">PremiAir VIP terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: PremiAir VIP terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Work began on PremiAir VIP terminal (adjacent to the Runway visitor park) in 2019<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> and it opened on 21 October 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Passengers are shuttled to their flight by limousine included within the service. Luggage and lounge access is an additional service offered.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights to and from Manchester:<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer Lingus</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Dublin_Airport" title="Dublin Airport">Dublin</a>\n</td></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus_UK" title="Aer Lingus UK">Aer Lingus UK</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Maintenance_bases">Maintenance bases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Maintenance bases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manchester Airport is the home to the engineering base of Jet2.com and, up until 23 September 2019, it was also the engineering base of the <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Cook_Group_Airlines" title="Thomas Cook Group Airlines">Thomas Cook Group Airlines</a>. Airlines such as Etihad Airways also have one of six maintenance bases worldwide in Manchester with their newly opened (2011) line maintenance facility.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Freight_Terminal">World Freight Terminal</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: World Freight Terminal">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:An-225-manchester-2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/An-225-manchester-2006.jpg/220px-An-225-manchester-2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/An-225-manchester-2006.jpg/330px-An-225-manchester-2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/An-225-manchester-2006.jpg/440px-An-225-manchester-2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3200" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:An-225-manchester-2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Antonov_An-225_Mriya" title="Antonov An-225 Mriya">Antonov An-225</a> at Manchester Airport in 2006</div></div></div>\n<p>Manchester Airport has a World Freight Terminal, serving cargo-only freighter services and cargo carried on regular passenger flights.<sup id="cite_ref-freight_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freight-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> It was opened in 1986, west of the original airfield. There are 5,500,000&#160;sq&#160;ft (510,000&#160;m<sup>2</sup>) of warehouse and office space on site, including a chiller unit for frozen products and a border inspection post. There are three aircraft maintenance hangars, with five transit sheds, operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Airways_World_Cargo" title="British Airways World Cargo">British Airways World Cargo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swissport" title="Swissport">Swissport Cargo</a>, Menzies World Cargo, and <a href="/wiki/Dnata_UK" title="Dnata UK">dnata UK</a>. There are over 100 freight forwarding companies on site.<sup id="cite_ref-freight_96-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-freight-96">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Freight throughput at the airport grew from 94,000 tonnes in 1997 to the peak at 165,000 tonnes in 2007, but then declined to around 93,000 tonnes in 2013, subsequently increasing to over 109,000 tonnes in 2016 making Manchester the fourth-busiest UK airport for freight behind London Heathrow, East Midlands, and <a href="/wiki/London_Stansted_Airport" title="London Stansted Airport">London Stansted</a> airports.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg/220px-Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg/330px-Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg/440px-Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="481" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_A538_tunnel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/A538_road" title="A538 road">A538 road</a> runs beneath both runways via two separate tunnels. Part of the road is exposed between both runways.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg/220px-Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg/330px-Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg/440px-Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2526" data-file-height="1680" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_new_control_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The new control tower, opened in June 2013, with a Thomson Airways Boeing 787 Dreamliner taxiing in at the end of its delivery flight.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg/220px-Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg/330px-Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg/440px-Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4930" data-file-height="2958" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_Fire_Service_Photo_Call_2015.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Manchester Airport Fire Service</div></div></div>\n<p>Manchester Airport has two parallel <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runways</a>. Runway 1 (23R/05L) 3,048&#160;m \xc3\x97&#160;45&#160;m (10,000&#160;ft \xc3\x97&#160;148&#160;ft) and Runway 2 (23L/05R) 3,200&#160;m \xc3\x97&#160;45&#160;m (10,499&#160;ft \xc3\x97&#160;148&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-aip_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aip-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> The parallel runways lie 390&#160;m (1,280&#160;ft) apart and staggered by 1,850&#160;m (6,070&#160;ft) so that landings can be conducted independently on one runway whilst takeoffs are conducted on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-vat_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-vat-97">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The original main runway, then designated 06/24 and initially 3,300&#160;ft (1,006&#160;m) in length,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> opened on 17 May 1937<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> when the airport was used as an <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> base and a military aircraft assembly centre. It was extended in stages from 1952, reaching its current length in 1981 to attract <a href="/wiki/Flight_length" title="Flight length">long-haul</a> international traffic. As demand and aircraft movements both increased during the mid-1990s, mainly due to the newly completed Terminal 2, the airport studied the option of a second full-length runway. A consultation process began and <a href="/wiki/Planning_permission" title="Planning permission">planning permission</a> was approved in 1997, with construction work starting the same year.\n</p><p>The second runway, initially designated 06R/24L,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> became operational on 5 February 2001<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> at a cost of \xc2\xa3172&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> and was the first full-length commercial runway to open in Britain for over 20 years.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_100-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-100">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> The site where the second runway was constructed was on the southern airfield boundary, which is near the village of <a href="/wiki/Styal" title="Styal">Styal</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Cheshire" title="Cheshire">Cheshire</a> countryside. The project was deemed controversial because of the destruction of natural wildlife habitats<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated6_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated6-101">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> and because of changes to flight paths to enable aircraft to fly in and out of the second runway. Aircraft landing from the southwest on to Runway 2 (05R) fly lower over the residential area of <a href="/wiki/Knutsford" title="Knutsford">Knutsford</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> As aircraft rarely land on to Runway 2 from the northeast (Runway 23L) or takeoff from Runway 2 to the northeast (Runway 05R) there has been no change to the path of aircraft over Heald Green, Cheadle and Stockport.\n</p><p>Planning permission for Runway 2 (23L/05R) permits use of both runways between the hours of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="tel:0600\xe2\x80\x932200">0600\xe2\x80\x932200</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> At night between the hours of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="tel:2200-0600">2200-0600</a> single runway operations based on Runway 1 (23R/05L) are used.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Exceptions are made for emergencies and planned maintenance. In practice, dual runway operations incorporating Runway 2 (23L/05R) are only used at peak demand, which is currently in the morning and then again between 1300-2000hrs.<sup id="cite_ref-Airport_extends_second_runway_opening_hours_to_cope_with_demand_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airport_extends_second_runway_opening_hours_to_cope_with_demand-103">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Most aircraft arriving into Manchester Airport use the <a href="/wiki/Instrument_landing_system" title="Instrument landing system">instrument landing system</a>, which in line with most other airports has a glide slope of 3 degrees equal to descending 318 feet per <a href="/wiki/Nautical_mile" title="Nautical mile">nautical mile</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The prevailing wind direction is westerly, so normally aircraft fly from northeast to southwest. In practice this means that normally aircraft land from the northeast over Stockport, <a href="/wiki/Cheadle,_Greater_Manchester" title="Cheadle, Greater Manchester">Cheadle</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Heald_Green" title="Heald Green">Heald Green</a>, and takeoff towards Knutsford. In dual runway operations aircraft will usually land on to Runway 1 (23R) and depart from Runway 2 (23L). When the wind direction changes, usually affecting 20% of movements per annum,<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> operations are reversed with aircraft landing from the southwest, lining up to the south over <a href="/wiki/Northwich" title="Northwich">Northwich</a> and over Knutsford and taking off towards Stockport.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> In dual runway operations aircraft will usually land on to Runway 2 (05R) and depart from Runway 1 (05L).<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> Sometimes, aircraft arriving into Manchester Airport are held in <a href="/wiki/Holding_(aeronautics)" title="Holding (aeronautics)">stacks</a>, usually in poor weather when the movement rate decreases.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> The airport has 3 stacks: DAYNE, MIRSI and ROSUN, each located approximately 15/20 miles from the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> DAYNE serves arrivals from the south, ROSUN from the north and east and MIRSI from the west.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> If you live within 20 miles of the airport, you will likely see and hear aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-MANRDS_99-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MANRDS-99">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Control_Tower">Control Tower</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Control Tower">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A new control tower was opened on 25 June 2013. At 60&#160;m tall, it is the UK\'s second tallest control tower, after London Heathrow and it replaces the old tower on top of Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Security">Security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Manchester Airport is policed by the <a href="/wiki/Greater_Manchester_Police" title="Greater Manchester Police">Greater Manchester Police</a> and Manchester Airport Fire Service. Several security-related incidents have occurred at the airport in recent years.\n</p>\n<ul><li>In 2002, a security firm successfully smuggled fake explosives, detonators and genuine firearms onto a flight.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In 2004, the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Whistleblower" title="Whistleblower">Whistleblower</a></i> programme revealed security failures at the airport, including faulty metal detectors and a lack of regular random baggage checks.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Many of the claims made on the programme were later discredited and much of the camera work was found to be misleading (filming from a raised footpath was used to suggest there was no security fence on the southern perimeter of the site)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2019)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>.</li>\n<li>In 2005, police used a <a href="/wiki/Taser" title="Taser">taser</a> on a man spotted acting suspiciously on the <a href="/wiki/Airport_apron" title="Airport apron">apron</a>, after he appeared to resist arrest.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 6 June 2006, Aabid Hussain Khan, 21, of <a href="/wiki/West_Yorkshire" title="West Yorkshire">West Yorkshire</a> and a 16-year-old boy were arrested at the airport and later charged under Section 57 of the <a href="/wiki/Prevention_of_Terrorism_Acts" title="Prevention of Terrorism Acts">Terrorism Act</a>, for conspiracy to murder and conspiracy to cause public nuisance by using poisons or explosives.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 24 July 2012, an 11-year-old boy went straight through security and managed to board the nearest boarding flight from security in T1, which was a Jet2 flight to Rome. Halfway through the flight one passenger reported him to the cabin crew, who then detained the boy at Rome and put him on the next flight back to Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 5 August 2014, a 47-year-old man was arrested after the pilot of a plane became aware of a potential explosive device on board. This turned out to be a hoax. As a result, Manchester Airport airfield operations were suspended for around 30 minutes whilst the man was led away by armed police. The incident required an escort from an <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">RAF</a> <a href="/wiki/Eurofighter_Typhoon" title="Eurofighter Typhoon">Typhoon</a> jet into Manchester.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In April 2015, the passengers arriving from Madrid on a Ryanair flight entered the UK without having their passports checked. A spokesman for the airport said it was the responsibility of the airline\'s handling agent to notify the <a href="/wiki/UK_Border_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="UK Border Force">UK Border Force</a> about flights from outside the UK.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>In November 2017, the passengers arriving on an EasyJet flight from Paris were mistakenly directed to departures rather than arrivals. The situation was caused by a door that was opened by a staff member, which led to the cross-contamination of arriving and departing passengers. The security breach resulted in delays and confusion, with a spokesman for the Department of Transport stating that it is the responsibility of airlines and airport operators to ensure passengers arriving in the UK are directed through the correct route.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_transport">Ground transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Ground transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Manchester_Airport_station.jpg/220px-Manchester_Airport_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Manchester_Airport_station.jpg/330px-Manchester_Airport_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Manchester_Airport_station.jpg/440px-Manchester_Airport_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4320" data-file-height="3240" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_Airport_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>TransPennine Express <a href="/wiki/British_Rail_Class_185" title="British Rail Class 185">Class 185</a> arriving at the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport railway station</a></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_interchange_station.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Manchester_interchange_station.png/220px-Manchester_interchange_station.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Manchester_interchange_station.png/330px-Manchester_interchange_station.png 1.5x,
