class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Manchester_interchange_station.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the future Manchester Airport could benefit from construction of a nearby high-speed rail station linking the airport with the South and Central Manchester</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rail">Rail</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Rail">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport station</a></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport_station" title="Manchester Airport station">Manchester Airport station</a>, opened in May 1993,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> is between Terminals 1 and 2. It is linked to the terminals by a <i>Skylink</i> moving walkway. Trains operated by <a href="/wiki/Northern_(train_operating_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern (train operating company)">Northern</a>, <a href="/wiki/TransPennine_Express" title="TransPennine Express">TransPennine Express</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transport_for_Wales_Rail_Services" title="Transport for Wales Rail Services">Transport for Wales</a> connect the airport to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Piccadilly_station" title="Manchester Piccadilly station">Manchester Piccadilly</a> and other railway stations, mainly throughout northern England, including <a href="/wiki/Crewe_railway_station" title="Crewe railway station">Crewe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wigan_North_Western_railway_station" title="Wigan North Western railway station">Wigan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Southport_railway_station" title="Southport railway station">Southport</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Waverley_railway_station" title="Edinburgh Waverley railway station">Edinburgh</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glasgow_Central_station" title="Glasgow Central station">Glasgow</a> in Scotland and <a href="/wiki/Holyhead_railway_station" title="Holyhead railway station">Holyhead</a> and <a href="/wiki/Llandudno_railway_station" title="Llandudno railway station">Llandudno</a> in Wales. A third platform was completed in 2008 to allow for an increase in rail capacity. In 2009, <a href="/wiki/Network_Rail" title="Network Rail">Network Rail</a> stated that the third platform meant that capacity will become constrained by the layover of the trains and recommended building a line underneath the Airport towards Northwich by 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> In January 2013, the Government announced that a new railway station, <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Interchange" title="Manchester Interchange">Manchester Interchange</a> on the north side of the M56 will be included in Phase 2 of <a href="/wiki/High_Speed_2" title="High Speed 2">High Speed 2</a> which will provide links with other British cities like Birmingham and London and also a quicker route into Central Manchester.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Work on building a new fourth platform at the existing railway station commenced in early 2014 with a blockade required in February 2015 to allow completion.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Construction finished in May 2015 and the platform opened to passengers in autumn 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metrolink">Metrolink</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Metrolink">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Airport_Line_(Manchester_Metrolink)" title="Airport Line (Manchester Metrolink)">Airport Line (Manchester Metrolink)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg/220px-Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg/330px-Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg/440px-Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tram_3074_at_Manchester_Airport_Metrolink_station.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A tram at Manchester Airport in November 2014 shortly after the line opened.</div></div></div>\n<p>A Metrolink service from <a href="/wiki/Cornbrook_tram_stop" title="Cornbrook tram stop">Cornbrook station</a> to the Airport opened in November 2014 and runs at 12-minute frequency. Journeys along the 15-stop line from Cornbrook take approximately 35 minutes. The <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Metrolink" title="Manchester Metrolink">Manchester Metrolink</a> light rail system has had plans to extend to the airport for many years. When the idea of a congestion charge was mooted, part of the scheme was to have extended the Metrolink to the airport. However, when this was rejected the future of the scheme was in doubt. In 2009, it was announced that the line to the airport would finally be built. The airport line is one spur of the line from <a href="/wiki/St_Werburgh%27s_Road_tram_stop" title="St Werburgh&#39;s Road tram stop">St Werburgh\'s Road</a>, to <a href="/wiki/East_Didsbury_tram_stop" title="East Didsbury tram stop">East Didsbury</a> and Manchester Airport, which opened on 3 November 2014 \xe2\x80\x93 18 months ahead of schedule.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> As of January 2018, Metrolink services from the Airport operate to <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Victoria_station#Victoria_tram_stop" title="Manchester Victoria station">Manchester Victoria</a> via <a href="/wiki/Market_Street_tram_stop" title="Market Street tram stop">Market Street</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_and_coach">Bus and coach</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Bus and coach">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><i>The Station</i> is the airport\'s ground transport interchange and brings <a href="/wiki/Bus_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Bus transport in the United Kingdom">bus</a>, <a href="/wiki/Coach_transport_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Coach transport in the United Kingdom">coach</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport_in_Great_Britain" title="Rail transport in Great Britain">rail</a> passengers under one roof. Over 300 trains, 100 coaches and 500 buses a day use the facility,<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> including the 24-hour bus service 43,<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> which runs every 10 minutes (every 30 minutes at night) to Manchester city centre via Wythenshawe, Northenden, Withington, Fallowfield and Rusholme. There is also <i>Skyline</i> service 199 operating every 30 minutes to Buxton via Stockport, Disley and Chapel-en-le-Frith, as well as a number of <a href="/wiki/Stagecoach_Manchester" title="Stagecoach Manchester">Stagecoach Manchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arriva_North_West" title="Arriva North West">Arriva North West</a> services to Stockport, Altrincham and various parts of South Manchester. A network of <a href="/wiki/National_Express_Coaches" title="National Express Coaches">National Express</a> and <a href="/wiki/Megabus_(Europe)" title="Megabus (Europe)">Megabus</a> coach services serve Manchester Airport and operate to destinations further afield.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Road">Road</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Road">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport is a 20-minute drive from Manchester city centre and is reached by the <a href="/wiki/M56_motorway" title="M56 motorway">M56 motorway</a>, with a dedicated <a href="/wiki/Spur_route" title="Spur route">approach road</a> from the motorway at junction 5. The M56 is the main route used by traffic to reach the airport. There are also minor local roads serving the airport from the north (<a href="/wiki/Wythenshawe" title="Wythenshawe">Wythenshawe</a>) and the east (<a href="/wiki/Heald_Green" title="Heald Green">Heald Green</a>). The M56/<a href="/wiki/A538_road" title="A538 road">A538 road</a> junction serves the World Freight Terminal, to the west of the airport. The A538 runs east\xe2\x80\x93west serving the local towns of <a href="/wiki/Altrincham" title="Altrincham">Altrincham</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wilmslow" title="Wilmslow">Wilmslow</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox current red Asia Australia.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/42px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png" decoding="async" width="42" height="34" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/63px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg/84px-Ambox_current_red_Asia_Australia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="290" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">Parts of this article (those related to Progress on SEMMMS) need to be <b>updated</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information. <br /><small>Last update: April 2016</small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Proposed as part of the SEMMMS (South East Manchester Multi-Modal Strategy) Relief Road Scheme, <a href="/wiki/A555_road" title="A555 road">a new link road</a> to the <a href="/wiki/A6_road_(England)" title="A6 road (England)">A6</a> south of Stockport opened in 2018. Planning permission had been granted, with inquiries for <a href="/wiki/Compulsory_purchase_order" title="Compulsory purchase order">Compulsory Purchase</a> and <a href="/wiki/Side_Roads_Order" title="Side Roads Order">Side Roads Orders</a> following up in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> After significant delays, the link road opened on 15 October 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Taxi ranks are situated by arrivals at all three terminals.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parking">Parking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Parking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The airport\'s official short-stay car parking can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Multistorey_car_park" title="Multistorey car park">multistorey car parks</a> adjacent to Terminals 1, 2 and 3. In July 2007 the airport introduced a \'No Waiting\' restriction on all access roads surrounding the terminals.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2018)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As of June 2018, the public are required to pay charges of \xc2\xa33 for five minutes on the terminal forecourt or \xc2\xa34 for the maximum ten minutes in order to drop off passengers. The charges have been highly controversial; local taxi drivers have described them as a "<a href="/wiki/Cash_cow" title="Cash cow">cash cow</a>" for the airport,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> and were described by a judge for Minshull Street Crown Court as "extraordinary" and "an absolute disgrace" after he gave a psychology teacher a suspended sentence for deliberately driving into a parking official in an act of <a href="/wiki/Road_rage" title="Road rage">road rage</a> over the charges.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2009/2010 Terminal 1\'s multi-storey car park was refurbished. Each level of the car park is colour-coded. The floor, walls, ceiling and supports have all received a repaint with every parking space having a sensor and green light above it, with empty parking bays indicated by the green light.\n</p><p>Official long-stay on-airport <a href="/wiki/Parking" title="Parking">parking</a> from Manchester Airport is located near the terminals and served by a regular courtesy bus. There is one long-stay car park serving Terminals 1 and 3 and a separate dedicated long-stay car park for Terminal 2. In 2009 the airport opened <i>JetParks</i> \xe2\x80\x93 two long-stay car parks less than a mile from the terminals. This is a cheaper alternative to the on-site car parks and is served by a 24-hour shuttle bus every 15 minutes. The airport also operates a <i>Shuttle Park</i> for long-stay car parking, which is also served by a regular courtesy bus and is located just off the airport site to the east of Terminal 3.\nThe airport has since augmented these products with a 3rd <i>JetParks</i> car park, <i>JetParks 3</i>. This is located adjacent to Shuttle Parks and as a result, Shuttle Parks was renamed <i>JetParks Plus</i>.\nManchester Airport also operates a very large scale <a href="/wiki/Valet_parking" title="Valet parking">valet parking</a> product across all 3 terminals that it has branded as "Meet &amp; Greet".<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2014 a new, 9000 space car park located underneath the approach to 23R was constructed, the first area of the site opened in the autumn. The remainder of the facility will open in time for summer 2015.\n</p><p>There are several privately operated car parks within a short distance of the airport, served by shuttle bus, as well as several off-site companies operating valet parking services.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Drop_off_zones">Drop off zones</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Drop off zones">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Up until 2018 cars dropping off passengers could do so outside terminals for free.  On 10 July 2018, Manchester Airport took the step of introducing a fee of \xc2\xa33 to \xc2\xa34 for vehicles dropping off passengers at terminals.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup> Alternatively, passengers being dropped off can be taken to an off-site car park from where a shuttle bus operates to the terminals. The airport issues fines of up to \xc2\xa3100 to vehicles which breach its terms and conditions for the drop off zones.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> The changes have been seen as unwelcome and nonconstructive by passengers and taxi drivers, with some saying they will boycott the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> The change has also attracted criticism from local Councillors in Cheshire, who point out that many places directly under Manchester Airport\'s flight paths don\'t have a direct <a href="/wiki/Public_transport" title="Public transport">public transport</a> link to the airport. While some other UK airports also have drop off charges Manchester Airport\'s charges are overall higher than those at any other airport.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effect_on_the_area">Effect on the area</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Effect on the area">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Unbalanced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="Ambox scales.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ambox_scales.svg/50px-Ambox_scales.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ambox_scales.svg/75px-Ambox_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Ambox_scales.svg/100px-Ambox_scales.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="620" data-file-height="620" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>may be <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:DUE" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:DUE">unbalanced</a> towards certain viewpoints</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve the article</a> or discuss the issue on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Manchester_Airport" title="Talk:Manchester Airport">talk page</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">September 2016</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>Between 1997 and 1999 three <a href="/wiki/Protest_camp" title="Protest camp">protest camps</a> were set up to oppose the building of the second runway, the felling of nearby trees on land owned by the <a href="/wiki/National_Trust_for_Places_of_Historic_Interest_or_Natural_Beauty" class="mw-redirect" title="National Trust for Places of Historic Interest or Natural Beauty">National Trust</a> in Styal, Cheshire and air transportation in general. Camps were set up in Flywood, Arthur\'s Wood<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> and Cedar\'s Wood. <a href="/wiki/Swampy_(environmentalist)" title="Swampy (environmentalist)">Swampy</a>, a well known activist, was among many protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> Much environmental damage was caused by the protesters disrupting measures to safely relocate wildlife (such as removing newt traps or fencing).\n</p><p>The south west end of the new runway is closer to the town of Knutsford and to the village of Mobberley. There was initially an increase in noise experienced by local residents from the aircraft being lower and closer.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated4_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated4-102">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> All residents that were able to prove that their property had lost value, as a result of the operation of Runway 2, were compensated in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup>\nIn 2012 Manchester Airports Group made a further, voluntary payment, to compensate those who felt aggrieved but had been unable to prove financial harm as a result of the operation of Runway 2. The precepts for Knutsford Town Council and Mobberley Parish Council residents were paid and money invested in local schools.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 Manchester Airport applied to build on land in Styal to increase its car parking. However, the former <a href="/wiki/Macclesfield_(borough)" title="Macclesfield (borough)">Macclesfield Borough Council</a> refused to give them planning permission to do so and expressed annoyance at the airport for not investing enough in public transport.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The decision seemed to many illogical as the same Council consistently failed to act to prevent private car parking businesses operating, in the same area, without planning permission. In a further bizarre twist in 2017/18 the successor to Macclesfield Borough Council, Cheshire East Borough Council, cut funding for the only bus service to Manchester Airport from their Council area. This removed the opportunity for 1,000s of their residents to access Manchester Airport through the bus service the Airport had established, and initially subsidised, in 2000.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Accidents_and_incidents">Accidents and incidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Accidents and incidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li>On 27 March 1951, a <a href="/wiki/Douglas_C-47_Skytrain" title="Douglas C-47 Skytrain">Douglas C-47A-75-DL Dakota 3</a> cargo aircraft operated by <a href="/wiki/Air_Transport_Charter" title="Air Transport Charter">Air Transport Charter</a><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> and en route to <a href="/wiki/RAF_Nutts_Corner" title="RAF Nutts Corner">Nutts Corner</a>, <a href="/wiki/County_Antrim" title="County Antrim">Antrim</a>, Northern Ireland, <a href="/wiki/1951_Ringway_Dakota_crash" title="1951 Ringway Dakota crash">crashed</a> at Heyhead shortly after take-off from runway 06, following the aircraft\'s failure to gain height. There were four fatalities \xe2\x80\x93 two of the three crew on board and two of the three passengers. The subsequent investigation found that the crash resulted from a loss of engine power, caused by ice forming in the <a href="/wiki/Carburetor" title="Carburetor">carburettor</a> intakes, attributable to the captain\'s failure to use the heat controls. An extended undercarriage and snow on the wings may have also been contributory factors.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 14 March 1957, <a href="/wiki/British_European_Airways" title="British European Airways">British European Airways</a> Flight "Bealine 411" operated by <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> 701 (registration G-ALWE) inbound from Amsterdam crashed into houses in Shadow Moss Road, Woodhouse Park. The aircraft was on final approach to Runway 24 at Manchester Airport and the crash was due to a flap failure, caused by fatigue of a wing bolt. All 20 occupants on board died, as did two on the ground.</li>\n<li>On 29 April 1957, a <a href="/wiki/Miles_Aerovan" title="Miles Aerovan">Miles Aerovan</a> Type 4 crashed on takeoff due to fuel pump failure. 2 on board were killed, including the pilot.</li>\n<li>On 4 June 1967, a <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-4" title="Douglas DC-4">Canadair C-4 Argonaut</a> (registration G-ALHG) was inbound from Palma and <a href="/wiki/Stockport_air_disaster" title="Stockport air disaster">crashed</a> near the centre of <a href="/wiki/Stockport" title="Stockport">Stockport</a> after loss of engine power due to fuel problems and an aborted approach to Manchester Airport, with 72 fatalities.</li>\n<li>On 20 March 1969, <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> G-AVJA of <a href="/wiki/British_Midland_International" title="British Midland International">British Midland International</a> crashed on take-off. Three of the four people on board were killed.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN200369_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN200369-139">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>On 22 August 1985, an engine of a <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737#737-200" title="Boeing 737">Boeing 737-236 Advanced</a>, operated by <a href="/wiki/British_Airtours" title="British Airtours">British Airtours</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airtours_Flight_28M" title="British Airtours Flight 28M">failed during take-off</a> from runway 24, the fire spreading into the cabin, resulting in 55 fatalities (mostly from smoke inhalation) aboard the Boeing 737-236 Advanced G-BGJL. The uncontained engine failure was later traced to an incorrectly repaired <a href="/wiki/Combustor" title="Combustor">combustor</a> causing the turbine disc to shatter and puncture the wing fuel tanks.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup> As a result, fire resistance and evacuation procedures were improved.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Runway_Visitor_Park">Runway Visitor Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Runway Visitor Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg/220px-Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg/330px-Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg/440px-Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="425" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Concorde_at_Manchester_Viewing_Park.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Concorde BOAC in its hangar at the Aviation Viewing Park.</div></div></div>\n<p>Manchester Airport has had public viewing areas since the airport opened to the public in 1938. The 1960/1970s pier-top viewing facilities have been closed because of security concerns. In May 1992, an official "Aviation Viewing Park" (AVP) was created just off the <a href="/wiki/A538_road" title="A538 road">A538 road</a> on the south-western side of the airfield. This was moved to the western side of the airfield in May 1997 to allow construction of the second runway.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> Renamed the "Runway Visitor Park" in June 2010, the facility is regarded as providing the best official viewing facilities for <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_spotting" title="Aircraft spotting">aircraft spotting</a> at any major UK airport by aircraft enthusiasts.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Visitors can view aircraft taking off and landing from both runways and aircraft taxiing to and from the runways. This attraction now draws around 300,000 visitors a year and is one of Greater Manchester\'s top 10 attractions.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Manchester_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-pax-91"><span domestic and international passengers</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-mov-92"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-mov_92-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a landings</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a
